## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the stress-strain-temperature constitutive relationship for a material. Stress typically increases with strain (hardening) and decreases with temperature (thermal softening), and classical models combine these effects multiplicatively or additively.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic regime)
- Temperature-dependent Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 - T) (linear elasticity with thermal softening of modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (plastic strain hardening, Hollomon equation)
- Power-law with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 - T)**c3 (combined hardening and softening)
- Johnson-Cook style: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 - c4 * T) (strain hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Ludwik model: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Thermally-activated Ludwik: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(c3 * T) (hardening with Arrhenius-type thermal term)
- Voce hardening with temperature: sigma = (c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon)) * (c3 - c4 * T) (saturating hardening with linear softening)
- Arrhenius thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (power-law hardening with exponential thermal dependence)
- Polynomial constitutive: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * T (quadratic strain with linear temperature)
- Swift model with temperature: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * (c3 - c4 * T) (offset power-law with thermal softening)
- Hyperbolic sine flow stress: sigma = c0 * asinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 * T)) (Garofalo/Sellars-Tegart type)
- Linear thermoelastic: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * T + c2 * epsilon * T (bilinear with cross-coupling term)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 + c2 * epsilon**(c3 - 1)) (nonlinear elastic-plastic)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening of elastic modulus → Stress proportional to (T_melt - T) or (1 - T*c) multiplicative factor
- Strain hardening saturation → Voce-type terms (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) that plateau at large strains
- Multiplicative decomposition → Stress = f(epsilon) * g(T), separable strain hardening and thermal softening
- Power-law strain hardening → epsilon**n with 0 < n < 1 indicates work-hardening behavior typical of metals
- Arrhenius temperature dependence → exp(-Q/(R*T)) or exp(c/T) indicates thermally-activated deformation mechanisms
- Yield stress offset → Additive constant c0 representing initial yield strength before hardening begins
- Homologous temperature scaling → Temperature appears as (T_ref - T) ratio reflecting distance from melting point
- Strain-temperature coupling → Product term epsilon*T indicates that hardening rate itself depends on temperature
